<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3b68dc2b-3fb7-418f-bd21-0d0198d4724b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer15310114125876889922">This masterpiece of modern comics storytelling brings to vivid life a dark world and an even darker man. Together with inker Klaus Janson and colorist Lynn Varley, writer/artist Frank Miller completely reinvents the legend of Batman in his saga of a near-future Gotham City gone to rot, ten years after the Dark Knight's retirement. <br/><br/>Crime runs rampant in the streets, and the</span>
  <span id="freeText15310114125876889922" style="display:none">This masterpiece of modern comics storytelling brings to vivid life a dark world and an even darker man. Together with inker Klaus Janson and colorist Lynn Varley, writer/artist Frank Miller completely reinvents the legend of Batman in his saga of a near-future Gotham City gone to rot, ten years after the Dark Knight's retirement. <br /><br />Crime runs rampant in the streets, and the man who was Batman is still tortured by the memories of his parents' murders. As civil society crumbles around him, Bruce Wayne's long-suppressed vigilante side finally breaks free of its self-imposed shackles. <br /><br />The Dark Knight returns in a blaze of fury, taking on a whole new generation of criminals and matching their level of violence. He is soon joined by this generation's Robin—a girl named Carrie Kelley, who proves to be just as invaluable as her predecessors.<br /><br />But can Batman and Robin deal with the threat posed by their deadliest enemies, after years of incarceration have made them into perfect psychopaths? And more important, can anyone survive the coming fallout of an undeclared war between the superpowers—or a clash of what were once the world's greatest superheroes?<br /><br />Over fifteen years after its debut, <i>Batman: The Dark Knight Returns</i> remains an undisputed classic and one of the most influential stories ever told in the comics medium.<br /><br />Collecting <i>Batman: The Dark Knight Returns</i> #1-4</span>

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317988i/689503.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b> OH, I GET IT NOW....THE JOKER IS SUPPOSED TO BE A PSYCHOTIC, HOMICIDAL MANIAC AND NOT AN UNDERSTUDY TO CHARLES NELSON REILLY</b><br><br><b> THANK YOU KIND SIR FOR RESTORING MY FAITH IN THE COMIC MEDIUM!!</b><br><br>OKAY, NUFF HISTORY....ON WITH THE REVIEW!!!<br><br>5.0 to 5.5 stars. One of the most influential graphic novels of all time, this amazing story single-handedly resurrected the character of Batman as "the Dark Knight" after the 70s and early 80s had turned him, thanks in large part to the success of the television show, into a light-hearted, campy hero (I refer you back to the history lesson above). This story pushed reset and Batman once again became the dark, fanatic, often ruthless character he was created to be. <br><br>As important as WHAT this graphic novel did for Batman specifically, it had an even greater impact on comics in general. Prior to the publication of “The Dark Knight Returns,” the entire comics industry was sagging and had lost a significant percentage of its fan base. The popularity of Frank Miller’s visionary work of this book led to a whole new era in comics. Following its success, comics saw the creation of very popular “anti-heros” like <i>Wolverine</i> and <i> the Punisher</i>, both of which were inspired by Miller’s version of the Dark Knight. In addition, the comic world began to see "darker, edgier" versions of classic characters being aimed at more mature audiences (e.g., Batman, Green Arrow, Daredevil, The Sandman). <br><br>In Summary, I would say that for all of its historical significance, the best reason to read this is that it is truly a great work of fiction and one that gets my HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION as it is....... <br><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&amp;current=fullofwin.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379751639i/135555.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> </span>

<div id="review_57664530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57664530" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57664530?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/20635071-batman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=recommended-by-a-not-stupid-friend">recommended-by-a-not-stupid-friend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57664530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1199190651062291455"><b>Because the best kind of <i>classic</i> has pictures...</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473942868ra/20534032.gif' width='300' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>So. I've actively (<i>and successfully</i>) avoided reading <b>TDKR</b> for many years now.<br/><i>Why, you ask?</i><br/>Well, to be honest, I was kinda <i>scared</i>. Now, if you aren't a comic book reader, then you might not understand how big of a deal this book is, but if you <i>are</i>...?<br/>Yeah,<i> you know.</i><br/>Which means, you're also aware of all the rabid comic nerds out there who go all stabby when you don't like their favorite character, publisher, title, bobblehead action figure...the lis</span>
  <span id="freeText1199190651062291455" style="display:none"><b>Because the best kind of <i>classic</i> has pictures...</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473942868ra/20534032.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So. I've actively (<i>and successfully</i>) avoided reading <b>TDKR</b> for many years now.<br><i>Why, you ask?</i><br>Well, to be honest, I was kinda <i>scared</i>. Now, if you aren't a comic book reader, then you might not understand how big of a deal this book is, but if you <i>are</i>...?<br>Yeah,<i> you know.</i><br>Which means, you're also aware of all the rabid comic nerds out there who go all stabby when you don't like their favorite character, publisher, title, bobblehead action figure...the list goes on.<br>Hey, I'm not judging! <i>I'm</i> one of those nerds. Believe me, I know how dangerous it can be to wade into <s>dork</s> shark infested waters.<br><b>And if (<i>God forbid</i>) I wrote a review saying I didn't like this?!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473945531ra/20534550.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I've picked this up from the library multiple times, flipped through it, stuck it in my bag, and then took it back to my local branch at my earliest convenience.<br>Because.<br><i>deep breath</i><br>Because of the <i>huge</i> amount of dialogue, and all those fucking Talking Heads!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473946812i/20534840._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I mean, <i>for real</i>, Miller? You're killing my tiny dinosaur brain with all of those <b>w<i>oooooo</i>rds</b>. <br>And the art? <i>Weeeeeell...</i><br>It's kinda ugly. &lt;--<b>personal opinion</b><br>Sometimes the characters look like they're lumpy or something. Perhaps Miller &amp; Janson envisioned a world where everyone was made of congealed oatmeal or cottage cheese?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473947526i/20534960._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br> <i>ducks, runs</i><br><b>Ok. Put your pitchforks down!</b><br><i>Jesbus. Touchy.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473947744ra/20534984.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Anyway, I ended up <i>finally</i> giving in, giving up, and giving <b>TDKR</b> a fair shot, <i>sigh</i> because my teenage son wanted to read it. Which, maybe wouldn't have been enough to turn the tide all by itself, but right around the same time (<i>serendipity?</i>) a friend here on Goodreads was kind enough to gift me a copy. <br><s>And then bug me till I read it.</s><br>Plus, after my son got done with it, he basically shoved it at me while making all these weird squealing fanboy noises. &lt;--please don't tell him I said that!<br>So.<br>I read it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473953685i/20536039._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And I really enjoyed it!</b><br>Whoduthunkit?! Not me, that's for sure. I assumed this would probably go down as one of those comics that I <i>had</i> to read, but didn't really <i>like</i>. <br>Sure, sure...its importance for Batman mythos<b> can't</b> be denied, but that doesn't always equal something that can stand the test of time. And it <i>especially</i> doesn't mean that someone with my pea-sized tolerance for dry/crunchy/old comics will savor the reading experience.<br>But I did.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473954359i/20536134.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a <i>great</i> Batman story, but not quite what I would call 5 star stuff in 2016. Those Heads just...<i>yeesh</i>, they almost did me in! The cluttered feel of so many of the pages kept me from wanting to linger, and the knobbly faces of the characters were (at times) a turnoff.<br><b>BUT</b>.<br>The story <i>itself</i> was fantastic. It was just as gritty and dark as I was promised, but there was also a glimmer of <i>hope</i> to it that I wasn't expecting.<br>It caught me off guard and made me smile.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473952747i/20535906._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Overall, I thought this was good stuff!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1199190651062291455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1865249683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1865249683" />
    <a title="Khurram" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25493797-khurram"><img alt="Khurram" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383996638p2/25493797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1865249683?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khurram" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khurram" href="/user/show/25493797-khurram">Khurram</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781563893421" href="/book/show/57948.Batman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1865249683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11097597969273429321">really enjoyed this comic; I keep wondering why it took me so long to read it. I finally got around to reading it after being blown away by Batman: The Dark Knight Returns, Part 1 (Region 2) and Batman: The Dark Knight Returns - Part 2 [DVD]. I thought it was finally time to get round to the source material. I am glad I did.<br/><br/>I quick recap of the story. Bruce is no longer Batman. There has been no Batman for 10 years. To curb his urges Bruce has become something of an adrenalin junkie study. Gotha</span>
  <span id="freeText11097597969273429321" style="display:none">really enjoyed this comic; I keep wondering why it took me so long to read it. I finally got around to reading it after being blown away by Batman: The Dark Knight Returns, Part 1 (Region 2) and Batman: The Dark Knight Returns - Part 2 [DVD]. I thought it was finally time to get round to the source material. I am glad I did.<br /><br />I quick recap of the story. Bruce is no longer Batman. There has been no Batman for 10 years. To curb his urges Bruce has become something of an adrenalin junkie study. Gotham has become a darker and more lawless place. On the 10 year anniversary of the last Batman sighting Bruce's subconscious "Batman" fights back telling him Bruce he is just the shell and he is not done with him yet.<br /><br />Most of what I though was great about the movies holds true to the comic, with a couple of exception. I have to say I prefer the animation of the movies, but I think at the time of the comic and for what is trying to be portrayed it does work. Meaning Batman strikes from the shadow leaving his opponent incapacitated and confused as to what just happened. A couple of the panels like when Batman takes out the pimp in the back of the taxi I it took me a while to see what happened from the art work. Like I said these were surgical strikes and it does put me in the mind of the pimp with a broken hand, thinking my hand is broken what just happened. When Batman decides to show himself the art work reflects that by drawing bigger more detailed pictures of him. The main thing I did not like about the comic was I thought there was too much of the talking heads. The media discussions of Batman, I can understand why this was done e.g. the Arkem psychologist taking an anti-batman stance to sell more of his book and make a name for himself, but I think it was a bit overdone. I mean all together this probably makes up half the contents of the book. The best think about the comic and it major advantage over the movies is the internal dialog Batman has with himself. In the movies they make Batman talk more to explain his methods. Whereas if you look at the comics there are very few speech bubbles while he is Batman and most of these are orders or threats. The rest of them it is Batman analysing everything in his head. I think that is what makes his scarier, (like when a magic trick is explained it is not as impressive), having the unknown factor is what Batman his edge. An example of this is in the second fight with the Mutant Leader, the Leader cannot understand Batman is targeting nerve clusters and showing him shallow cuts in the "just the right" places can be effective. I also like the way he keep thinking lucky with every near miss, and the explanation of why he paints a big bright target on his chest. I also like the way Batman has evolved, he is not above using guns, will kill to protect given no other option, and lacing his smoke bombs with a watered down version of the scarecrows fear gas is genius, not only does he appear in front of his victims, he appears in front of them as their "worst nightmares"!<br /><br />The others, Commissioner Garden is still Batman's biggest supporter but is facing retirement it is not really until he is gone that Batman man realises how much Garden protected him. Garden is the same tough but fair cop he always was. The Joker is just as evil as ever he comes out of his coma with the return of Batman and makes one last mass murdering run at Gotham. Unlike in the movie the Joker is not a physical match for Batman, but is a master of psychologically pushing his buttons. He knows this is his last chance if you will and he wants to die at the hands of Batman. Superman has become a tool of the establishment. Batman says it is because of Clarks respect for people in authority, but he also says to Clark nobody could force Clark to do something he did not want to do. Strangely Oliver and Clark share the same opinion on Batman he is too loud, he plays things mysterious but a loud kind of mysterious. Clark in his thought also says Batman need to work more in secret like he is force to do. This could be why he does not let anyone see him when he comes to Gotham. Maybe he should do something about his costume if he is trying to keep a low profile. The only thing I do not like it the relationship between Bruce and Alfred. Alfred is still the dutiful servant, but that is what Bruce seem to treat him like in this story a servant, someone to tell what to do and expect it to be done nothing more nothing less. Having said that Alfred does manage to get in some verbal barbs of his own, and though Bruce values his opinion probably more than anyone else's but there is a clear line saying Bruce/Batman is in charge live with it.<br /><br />I great comic , very detailed excellent as a standalone or as a companion to the movies to fill in extra details. A true classic for Batman fans. Enjoy reading it repeatedly over multiple sittings it is a lot to take in. All good!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11097597969273429321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2097947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2097947" />
    <a title="Missy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/118599-missy"><img alt="Missy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181098121p2/118599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2097947?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Missy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Missy" href="/user/show/118599-missy">Missy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781563893421" href="/book/show/57948.Batman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118599-missy?shelf=graphicnovels">graphicnovels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2097947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16252842235361315115">When I was growing up, comic books (this was years before 'graphic novels') were frowned upon in my household, but I was addicted to them anyway. X-Men, to be precise, because, OMG, Jean Grey was smart and tough (at least until Dark Phoenix) AND had both Scott Summers and Wolverine in love with her. (I do love a good soap.) Batman was a joke back then, thanks to that moronic TV show. But Batman, the real Dark Knight, wasn't a joke--if Superman is who America yearns to be; Batman is who we're afr</span>
  <span id="freeText16252842235361315115" style="display:none">When I was growing up, comic books (this was years before 'graphic novels') were frowned upon in my household, but I was addicted to them anyway. X-Men, to be precise, because, OMG, Jean Grey was smart and tough (at least until Dark Phoenix) AND had both Scott Summers and Wolverine in love with her. (I do love a good soap.) Batman was a joke back then, thanks to that moronic TV show. But Batman, the real Dark Knight, wasn't a joke--if Superman is who America yearns to be; Batman is who we're afraid we are.<br /><br />In 1986, Frank Miller (Sin City) blew all of the camp out of the water and reclaimed a bit of popular culture by writing a stunning Batman and, not so incidentally, a picture-perfect example of why graphic novels aren't for kids. The artwork is fabulous, the characters are crisp and complex. It's not just the original Dark Knight, it's who that character evolved into. Dark, twisted, bitter, but still fighting to make things better. The movie Batman Begins never would have been made without this Dark Knight. Your library probably has a copy of this; check it out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16252842235361315115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3810060713581887731">I know I'm alone in this, but I didn't really like The Dark Knight Returns. I struggled with the story structure -- all the perspective switching left me frequently scratching my head to figure out who was speaking, where we were, and what the Heck was happening. I was confused by some characters (the guy with the freaky flying baby bombs?). I was bothered that there was no discussion of Ellen/Robin's family -- we have VERY little information on her or why she wants to join Bats, how she really </span>
  <span id="freeText3810060713581887731" style="display:none">I know I'm alone in this, but I didn't really like The Dark Knight Returns. I struggled with the story structure -- all the perspective switching left me frequently scratching my head to figure out who was speaking, where we were, and what the Heck was happening. I was confused by some characters (the guy with the freaky flying baby bombs?). I was bothered that there was no discussion of Ellen/Robin's family -- we have VERY little information on her or why she wants to join Bats, how she really proves that she's worthy, etc. She shows up in costume one day and he decides she's good enough? Hrmph. I don't buy it.<br /><br />Eh. I just found myself laboring through it rather than enjoying it. In contrast, I loved The Long Halloween. I look forward to reading Dark Knight Year One to see if I like that any better.</span>

</a><br><br><b>This is a totally different spin on Batman first published in 1986 by Frank Miller. </b><br><br>Don't expect it to be like the old cartoons. <br><br>Definitely not like the Adam West Batman from the 60s. <br><br>Not the Justice League of America. <br><br>Batman and Superman are hardly on speaking terms. The governments have passed laws against vigilante super heroes so most of them are in prison or banished, or, like Superman, secretly working for the government. <br><br>Batman, after a series of traumatic incidents, has not been seen in the last ten years. The Joker and Two Face are both in psycho wards. <br><br>A series of incidents force Batman to come back out to the shock of the world. Gotham is turned on its head and the public isn't sure what to make of him; especially the younger people who thought he was just a legend. <br><br>img src=<a href="http://s1077.photobucket.com/albums/w474/shannon20125/?action=view&amp;current=greatbatman03.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a>/&gt;<br><br>In this Batman faces off with two-face, the joker and a mutant gang which has practically overrun the streets. <br><br>Look for a face off against Superman, an intro. from the new Robin and a setup for the next book in the series, where Batman decides to free some of the super heroes in prison. <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/fGllZx1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363330i/714596._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

A sequel written and illustrated by Miller, The Dark Knight Strikes Again, was published in 2001. <br><br>Miller said that the comic series' plot was inspired by Dirty Harry, specifically the 1983 film Sudden Impact, in which Dirty Harry returns to crime-fighting after a lengthy convalescence. Miller also said his own increasing age was a factor in the plot. <div id="review_3302945337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3302945337" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7202176-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324164999p2/7202176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3302945337?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/7202176-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3302945337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17140683862573270979">It's one of the definitive Batman stories! It's brilliant! It helped comics become more serious! I hate it!<br/><br/>Hello everyone, welcome to another edition of Tim has an unpopular opinion.<br/><br/>Okay, so that last one is an exaggeration, I do not hate the Dark Knight Returns, but I do not like it, and I certainly do not love it like so many do.<br/><br/>Let's get this started with the direction most people seem to go with, I do not like Frank Miller. There has been plenty said about how Miller has become a self-parody</span>
  <span id="freeText17140683862573270979" style="display:none">It's one of the definitive Batman stories! It's brilliant! It helped comics become more serious! I hate it!<br><br>Hello everyone, welcome to another edition of Tim has an unpopular opinion.<br><br>Okay, so that last one is an exaggeration, I do not hate the Dark Knight Returns, but I do not like it, and I certainly do not love it like so many do.<br><br>Let's get this started with the direction most people seem to go with, I do not like Frank Miller. There has been plenty said about how Miller has become a self-parody of his work and how Sin City ruined his writing and that it's hard to enjoy his older work because of this. I'm not going that direction, though I honestly see where that group comes from.<br><br>I disliked this book before I disliked Miller. I'll also say something that most people who dislike Miller won't say; I genuinely enjoy some of his Sin City work (not all of them, but I've read them all and actually do think there are some gems). I dislike this book for four main reasons:<br><br>1. The art. I hate, genuinely hate, the art style. The story could be amazing, but it would be hard to get over a three star review simply for the art. It's ugly to look at. It's blocky, it's cramped because of the small panels and it's unimpressive all around. I know this is very much on opinionated thing, but this style worked better in Miller's later black and white style because the panels were frequently larger and less detail actually made the issues less obvious. It's unpleasant on the eyes and it legitimately gave me a headache.<br><br>2. TV talking heads. Oh yes, I know he gets worse with this later, but it was annoying attempt at political comedy here and adds very little to the actual story. <br><br>3. I dislike Superman as a character, always have and most likely always will, but even I will say that Miller is just ridiculous with his portrayal of him. Superman is guided by a moral compass, he should not be portrayed as an ineffectual tool for the government. He may be "all American," but his loyalty to the government (as shown many times) would not stretch to the lengths Miller goes to. He's a joke here, just to show how "awesome" Batman is in comparison. <br><br>4. Swastika pastie woman. Jesus Christ Frank, I don't even have words, but maybe the Joker does...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587941490i/29362786.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>(Made even funnier by the fact that she is supposed to work with the Joker... obviously other comic creators disagree with Miller’s take.)<br><br>Now, I won't disregard the merit of this book in terms of the history of comics. It did help get comics to be taken more seriously, it did help people think of Batman as the Dark Knight rather than Adam West and it did help usher in more interesting stories involving Superheroes. I also admit that I genuinely liked Carrie Kelley's story line about becoming Robin. <br><br>I like nothing else... okay, that's a lie. I love that one of the Mutant members says "It's just a Goddamned bat." <br><br>Because well, <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587929345i/29361549.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Thanks Miller, you added to your meme retroactively. <br><br>2/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17140683862573270979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_18718131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18718131" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18718131?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781563893421" href="/book/show/57948.Batman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sick-and-twisted">sick-and-twisted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=generally-overrated">generally-overrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=pissed-me-off">pissed-me-off</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=popular-culture">popular-culture</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18718131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6814576120786895683">More often than not <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59960.Batman_The_Dark_Knight_Returns' title='Batman The Dark Knight Returns by Frank Miller' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Knight Returns</a> is considered one of the greatest graphic novels -- if not <u>the</u> greatest. I can't deny its importance to the form (and to the myth of Batman -- responsible as it is for Bruce Wayne's shift into the "Dark Knight" era), but having taught it a handful of times and read it for "pleasure" a few more (this reading having been prompted by Christopher Nolan's disappointing trilogy capper, The Dark Knight Rises) I feel that it is a vastly overrated work.<br/><br/>And Frank Mi</span>
  <span id="freeText6814576120786895683" style="display:none">More often than not <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59960.Batman_The_Dark_Knight_Returns" title="Batman The Dark Knight Returns by Frank Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Knight Returns</a> is considered one of the greatest graphic novels -- if not <u>the</u> greatest. I can't deny its importance to the form (and to the myth of Batman -- responsible as it is for Bruce Wayne's shift into the "Dark Knight" era), but having taught it a handful of times and read it for "pleasure" a few more (this reading having been prompted by Christopher Nolan's disappointing trilogy capper, The Dark Knight Rises) I feel that it is a vastly overrated work.<br /><br />And Frank Miller is delusional. <br /><br />In fact, I will go so far as to suggest that we're damn lucky Frank Miller can express himself in words and pictures (and get rich doing it) because if he couldn't express himself artistically (or was a failed artist like a certain Viennese painter), I'd put money on him walking into a theatre or a Sikh temple or a political round table and opening fire.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59960.Batman_The_Dark_Knight_Returns" title="Batman The Dark Knight Returns by Frank Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Knight Returns</a> is an ugly manifesto for vigilantism; it is the mad nightmare of a right wing kook who sees the world in ways that it simply isn't; it is an apologia for the first strike; it offers chaos and evil and calls it anarchy without any understanding of what anarchy is; it is a jingoistic, Soviet-era piece of Cold War propaganda; it is an attempt to rationalize violence as the proper response to violence; it attempts to reinforce the myth that a "good man" (or country?) can do bad things to bad people and the act cannot, therefore, be bad; yet it offers the tools to undermine and deconstruct the delusions of its author with what seems to be total obliviousness.<br /><br />There is no depth to the characters in this book. Batman is an ugly thug, a giant meat head, a bludgeon, a nasty beast of a man who revels in the torture and maiming of the "evil" denizens of Gotham. He's the ultimate rich bully, the bully who gets away with his bullying -- even today in our hyper-aware bullying police state -- the bully whose bullying is "okay" because it is targeted at other bullies or because the bully is too beautiful and rich and popular to really be a bully. Miller's Dark Knight isn't complex in any way -- certainly not in the way many of his antecedents have achieved. He is ugly and nothing more. His parents died violently, so he became a weapon against criminals. It's as shallow as it is simple. <br /><br />Miller also gives us the shabbiest expression of Superman ever to hit the comics. Just like the Batman, there's no complexity to the Man of Steel. He's a Boy Scout who follows the law and does what he's told by his leaders, so he's a target for Miller's ham-fisted criticism. Miller tells us Superman is weak and less than Batman because he can't do what must be done the way Batman can. Superman doesn't torture and maim; Superman doesn't kill; hence, Superman is a pussy. <br /><br />I closed the cover of this book moments before I started writing this review, and I can tell you that it's been a long time since I've felt so disgusted by the work of an author. It gets worse for me each time I read this, but like a moth banging into a window I can't stop returning to this, trying to see what I miss that everyone else sees. My disgust gets worse each time I read it, yet I can't stop my examination of how this nasty tale could have led to our fascination with The Dark Knight. How could an idea that has had some truly excellent manifestations (such as Nolan's <i>Batman Begins</i> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/32594.Jeph_Loeb" title="Jeph Loeb" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeph Loeb</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6375845.Batman_Hush" title="Batman Hush by Jeph Loeb" rel="nofollow noopener">Batman Hush</a>) come from such awful source material? How can people like this book? What the hell am I missing? It's a mystery that only the World's Greatest Detective could solve. Too bad he was nowhere to be found in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59960.Batman_The_Dark_Knight_Returns" title="Batman The Dark Knight Returns by Frank Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Knight Returns</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6814576120786895683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20636734" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20636734" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20636734?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2019-comics">2019-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20636734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14320926866741418027">Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, Gotham is overrun by crime.<br/>Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, Commissioner James Gordon is retiring.<br/>Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, the world is on the brink of nuclear war.<br/>Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, Bruce Wayne has had enough!<br/>Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, The Dark Knight Returns!<br/><br/>The first time I read The Dark Knight Returns, I was an impressionable lad of twenty. Now, two decades later</span>
  <span id="freeText14320926866741418027" style="display:none">Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, Gotham is overrun by crime.<br />Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, Commissioner James Gordon is retiring.<br />Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, the world is on the brink of nuclear war.<br />Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, Bruce Wayne has had enough!<br />Ten years after the last appearance of Batman, The Dark Knight Returns!<br /><br />The first time I read The Dark Knight Returns, I was an impressionable lad of twenty. Now, two decades later, I've revisited it.<br /><br />The Dark Knight Returns is still a powerful book. Bruce Wayne crawls out of a bottle, shaves off his mustache, and puts on the cowl to fight crime once again, heading toward inevitable showdowns with Joker and Superman once he restores order to the streets of Gotham.<br /><br />The art shows the evolution of Frank Miller's style from his Daredevil days, bridging the gap between that style and the style he'd be known for on Sin City years later. The writing is why the book was influential at the time, though, and is still influential decades later. This is the birth of the chronically pissed off, over-planning Batman of today. It also paved the way for Batman: Year One, the Tim Burton Batman movie, and even Batman Beyond to some degree. Broken down Batman in this volume isn't that far removed from broken down Batman in Batman Beyond.<br /><br />I'm a sucker for tales of the aging hero trying to fix things while he still can and that's pretty much what this story is. However, this book has not aged nearly as well as Watchmen or even Miller's own Batman: Year One. It screams 1980s on almost every page. I also forgot how damn wordy it is.<br /><br />For good or for bad, Batman: The Dark Knight Returns is an influential Batman book and an important piece of Batman lore. However, I don't think it holds up nearly as well as Batman: Year One or Batman: The Killing Joke. 3.75 out of 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14320926866741418027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16680809077894734263">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>2.5 Stars<br/><br/>Egads, I think this is going to be really long. Sorry : (<br/><br/>My first superhero graphic novel review. It’s like diving right into shark infested waters. Please be gentle and keep in mind that I hold <b>zero</b> belief that anyone should ever take my reviews seriously. Period. But even more so when it comes to this one.<br/><br/>As I said, this is my first foray into the unchartered waters of the world of Batman other than through television and fi</span>
  <span id="freeText16680809077894734263" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>2.5 Stars<br><br>Egads, I think this is going to be really long. Sorry : (<br><br>My first superhero graphic novel review. It’s like diving right into shark infested waters. Please be gentle and keep in mind that I hold <b>zero</b> belief that anyone should ever take my reviews seriously. Period. But even more so when it comes to this one.<br><br>As I said, this is my first foray into the unchartered waters of the world of Batman other than through television and film. I chose <i>Batman: The Dark Knight Returns</i> for two reasons – I’m a Frank Miller fan and . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420821142ra/13272403.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420821142ra/13272404.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Yep. I’ve run the gamut with the a lot of you through this Batman . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420821142ra/13272405.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and this one . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420821142ra/13272406.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420821142ra/13272407.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>NO!</b><br><br>but this one . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420821142ra/13272408.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and even this one . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420821142ra/13272409.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Many claim all of the above were made possible because of this story. I’m obviously not an expert, so I have no clue if that’s true, but I’m going with it because that makes my first <i>Batman</i> selection so much cooler.<br><br>So why the “meh” rating? Wellllll, there are a few reasons. <br><br>First, Batman’s voice. I realize Batman has been out of commission for quite some time at the onset of this story and he has to work out the kinks while battling evil, but did his voice have to sound so much like this guy????<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272410._SY540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Miller left me having a chicken and egg moment for quite some time with that one. <br><br>Second, the artwork. Although sometimes Frank Miller’s simplistic artsy-fartsy style that I enjoy <i>really</i> showed on the page . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272411._SY540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and occasionally there were striking full-page images that kind of knocked my socks off . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272412._SY540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(Also, ‘Murica)<br><br>Unfortunately, there was also an abundance of pages with half-assed “television screens” taking place of actual art.<br><br>Speaking of those t.v. screens, that brings me to my final issue - the muddy storyline. Batman takes a back-up role to all of the ranty news reports discussing various political stances. (Sidenote to address those rants: This story was written nearly <b>30</b> years ago and the social injustices discussed in the storyline are the same ones happening today. FFS – get your shit together, America!) It got to be sooooo repetitive – almost like entire pages were copied/pasted. Between the news reports, Batman moaning about his aches and pains, and the bad guy mutants reminding me how they were going to “raze Gotham” and “rape the women” and “bathe in Gotham’s blood” every third page I found my attention wandering more than a time or two.<br><br>All that being said, there were some good points. The obvious being my familiarity with the basic story and Frank Miller. But also? The cameos. They were a fun little Easter egg hunt. Everyone from Letterman . . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272413._SY540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>to Ronald Reagan and Chris Christie (?) and . . . Hank Hill (?????) . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272414._SX540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>to Patrick Swayze and Keanu Reeves . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272415._SX540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I keeed, I keeeed.<br><br>Leaving my final experience with <i>Batman: The Dark Knight Returns</i> as definitely not one of the worst things I’ve ever subjected myself to.<br><br>Oh, and in case you’re wondering how a super professional comic book aficionado like myself prepares for a review like this, here’s a glimpse of my little world ; )<br><br>First, make sure you show you can prove you are a legit nerd by gathering your various Batman Pop Vinyls together . . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272416._SX540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then take one of your besties shopping for some Batman gear . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272417._SX540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br>(Dear Hot Topic, you can start sending me free crap whenever you feel like it in exchange for all these endorsements.)<br><br>Third, enlist the help of your resident Dark Knight to assist you in making sure you are providing well-thought out opinions . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272418._SY540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And finally, humiliate the other butthole who lives in your house and refuses to let you read anything containing colored or slick pages because he <i>insists</i> on laying on them all the time by making him wear a <s>B</s>Catman costume . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>See what happens when you act an ass, Django? I share your punishment with all of the interwebs.<br><br>One final note: What’s up with the nipples on those mutants???<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420821142i/13272420._SY540_.jpg" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Do they sit around breastfeeding each other all day when they aren’t raping women and bathing in their blood???<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16680809077894734263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_126127554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126127554" />
    <a title="Buck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1450485-buck"><img alt="Buck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345474554p2/1450485.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126127554?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Buck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Buck" href="/user/show/1450485-buck">Buck</a>
      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10034182292909153955">What a mess! <br/><br/>Most pages had 4 lines of 4 pictures with dialogue above it. Much of the story was told through the media and news, which is a boring device when used this much. There was some great art, but so much of it was tiny and we did not get landscapes. <br/><br/>I also thought the story thread was choppy and things were slopped together. What was Superman doing in this. Dots are not connected and some things don't make sense. Batman is also old here. Robin is around, but not the Robin we know, but a</span>
  <span id="freeText10034182292909153955" style="display:none">What a mess! <br /><br />Most pages had 4 lines of 4 pictures with dialogue above it. Much of the story was told through the media and news, which is a boring device when used this much. There was some great art, but so much of it was tiny and we did not get landscapes. <br /><br />I also thought the story thread was choppy and things were slopped together. What was Superman doing in this. Dots are not connected and some things don't make sense. Batman is also old here. Robin is around, but not the Robin we know, but a girl. Batman is like an old grizzled grumpy man, which I liked that choice, it's unusual, but it got old toward the end. <br /><br />I had this on my list to read because it's a classic and people love it. I love a darker Batman, he is supposed to be dark, in my opinion, but I thought this story was sloppy, messy and it was not enjoyable to read at all. There were new things here, but I just didn't care. I see I'm in the minority, but I did not like this. It is not for me, simple as that. I'm glad others appreciate this, but I can't join in on that opinion. </span>

<div id="review_2343014086" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2343014086" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2343014086?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2343014086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9297030291687129272">Kids, remember: always be yourself. <br/><br/>Unless you can be Batman. <br/><br/>Always be Batman.<br/><br/>Incredibly, I did not LOVE this.<br/><br/>I liked it, no doubt. The IDEA of an aging Batman donning the cape and cowl, kicking creeps ass and then needing a rubdown later, picking a fight he could not win only to get up, dust off his old and tired self and BE the Dark Knight again was great. Miller is a genius and there were parts of this that reminded me of Alan Moore’s CLASSIC <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/472331.Watchmen' title='Watchmen by Alan Moore' rel='nofollow noopener'>Watchmen</a>, with it’s subtle and not so subtle poli</span>
  <span id="freeText9297030291687129272" style="display:none">Kids, remember: always be yourself. <br><br>Unless you can be Batman. <br><br>Always be Batman.<br><br>Incredibly, I did not LOVE this.<br><br>I liked it, no doubt. The IDEA of an aging Batman donning the cape and cowl, kicking creeps ass and then needing a rubdown later, picking a fight he could not win only to get up, dust off his old and tired self and BE the Dark Knight again was great. Miller is a genius and there were parts of this that reminded me of Alan Moore’s CLASSIC <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/472331.Watchmen" title="Watchmen by Alan Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">Watchmen</a>, with it’s subtle and not so subtle political and social commentary.<br><br>But the art was … eh.<br><br>And it was sometimes hard to follow.<br><br>Here’s the thing: what Miller did exceptionally well, over the top good, top shelf SCOTCH (I’m talking 12 year old McCallans) was to further humanize DC’s most human, and therefore most compelling hero. How better to explore our hero’s humanity than to delve into his MORTALITY, he’s getting OLD. But he’s still a hero, and still dark, still pissed off and still wants to not only get the bad guy, but punish him, beat the shite out of him and make it really hurt.<br><br>This is like if Batman were Rocky Balboa. Not the 1976 version, a young warrior; this Batman is the Rocky Balboa of the same film name in 2006, old and coming out of retirement, and like the Toby Keith song: not as good as he once was, but he's as good once as he ever was.<br><br>A more observant and inspired reviewer than me once noted that Marvel had humans who were striving to be gods; DC had gods struggling to be human. My problem with DC has always been the Superman paradigm: he’s too powerful, he NEEDS weakness to be more accessible and thus more interesting as a hero.<br><br>Miller gets into this some as Superman (noticeably NOT getting older) is shown still doing the incredible and hardly believable (though with some fresh ECO sensibilities) and has an almost satirical approach to Batman and Superman’s complicated relationship and that makes this all the more absorbing.<br><br>Probably a MUST read for genre fans, and still a damn fine story on many levels.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1523069354i/25337734._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9297030291687129272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_209319037" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/209319037" />
    <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington"><img alt="Jonathan Terrington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478230200p2/6313408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/209319037?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Terrington" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington">Jonathan Terrington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=want">want</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=personal-favourites">personal-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer209319037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13790642771747562675"><br/>Before Christopher Nolan came alone and further redefined the idea of superheroics, Frank Miller was doing well enough to keep Batman fresh and interesting in his own way. <i>The Dark Knight Returns</i> tops my list of best graphic novels ever written for what it did for the genre, what it did for Batman and what it stands as today. Though <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/472331.Watchmen' title='Watchmen by Alan Moore' rel='nofollow noopener'>Watchmen</a> is universally accepted as the greatest graphic novel I personally believe this is greater in that it was written previously and from what I've read appears</span>
  <span id="freeText13790642771747562675" style="display:none"><br />Before Christopher Nolan came alone and further redefined the idea of superheroics, Frank Miller was doing well enough to keep Batman fresh and interesting in his own way. <i>The Dark Knight Returns</i> tops my list of best graphic novels ever written for what it did for the genre, what it did for Batman and what it stands as today. Though <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/472331.Watchmen" title="Watchmen by Alan Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">Watchmen</a> is universally accepted as the greatest graphic novel I personally believe this is greater in that it was written previously and from what I've read appears to have 'opened the door' for <i>Watchmen</i> to become so accepted.<br /><br />This is not the glossy Batman of the television shows, movies or recent comics. This is the ultimate representation of Batman as the Dark Knight. As a man straddling the line between hero and vigilante, as a man with a dark past he keeps running from and with villains who rise up against his heroic light. He is a man who keeps running from his past but can never escape the fact of the legend and icon he is. No wonder recent Doctor Who writers noted that there was a sense of Batmanification about the Doctor's latest incarnation. In short this novel fully explores many of the deep philosophical and psychological aspects of who and what Batman is as a symbol.<br /><br />Essentially this is a semi-dystopian novel in graphic form. A tale of what happens when governments allow crime to run rampant, when superheroes are outlawed and when the Batman returns. Because essentially that is what the Batman is, a figure outside of the law who can do the things the law should but cannot.<br /><br />The artwork is not neat or beautiful as some artwork is. But it fits the story perfectly, providing a further dark, gritty and rough edge to complement the plot. And that is what strong artwork should do in a graphic novel, it should fit the story rather than try and bedazzle the reader into believing the story is strong. Frank Miller certainly appears to have understood how to make a piece of art which is edgy and gives you both barrels in its artwork and story.<br /><br />The story features an older Batman returning to action in Gotham - hence the title. But this is a Gotham devoid of the heroes of the past, this is a Gotham where heroes do not live. This is the dark incarnation of Gotham, a city of crime. And therefore Batman returns, a legend come to haunt the criminals of the city. And rising up alongside him is a new, female version of Robin. <br /><br />The real theme of the story explores the idea of the hero or the vigilante. It questions whether, when evil and similarly chaos arise, a hero and order also arise. In the case of this novel, this hero is naturally Batman. The question is also raised that when one devotes oneself to fighting evil so incessantly if there is a cost, and the idea that Batman is a man who fights on only to keep running is again brought up.<br /><br />This is a masterpiece and if you are into graphic novels a must read work. If you are wanting to begin reading Batman, here is as good a place as any to begin, because Frank Miller (genius that he is) takes the essence of what Batman is and spins it out into a new and gritty setting, while also exploring deep themes. In this regard this work is literature because it combines thematic expression with imagery. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13790642771747562675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51289-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422281802p2/51289.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33214942?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/51289-katie">Katie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33214942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9750590486468272029">I'm sorry. I'm really sorry. I know that this is one case where there must be something wrong with *me* and not with the book, because it's been lauded as one of the greatest graphic novels in superhero history, and I thought it sucked.<br/><br/>The story is very difficult to follow - and this coming from someone who is well-versed in Batman lore, and who is used to the comic book medium for storytelling. Poor writing.<br/><br/>The pictures are sometimes difficult to interpret - it's hard to even figure out what's </span>
  <span id="freeText9750590486468272029" style="display:none">I'm sorry. I'm really sorry. I know that this is one case where there must be something wrong with *me* and not with the book, because it's been lauded as one of the greatest graphic novels in superhero history, and I thought it sucked.<br /><br />The story is very difficult to follow - and this coming from someone who is well-versed in Batman lore, and who is used to the comic book medium for storytelling. Poor writing.<br /><br />The pictures are sometimes difficult to interpret - it's hard to even figure out what's being depicted. This is unfortunate, especially when you know it's a panel that's supposed to be conveying something extremely a) emotional/moving, or b) important to the story.<br /><br />Finally, a personal opinion, which only affects my review insomuch as ratings are partially based on personal taste: I liked Batman the way he was before Frank Miller "reinvented" him. I do not like this bitter, cranky old man Batman who gets pleasure from hurting people. I like the heroic old-fashioned Batman who hurts bad guys simply because they're bad guys and he's the good guy. Like I said, it's just a matter of personal taste.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9750590486468272029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
